DRAM was generally 1/4 the price per bit of SRAM (because 1/4 the die size), but if you didn't use quite a bit of DRAM in a machine, the cost savings of the DRAM was offset by the cost of the additional support electronics required. While the difficulty of interfacing DRAM in general, and the 1103 specifically, was in my opinion greatly overstated, using static RAM was definitely easier, which is presumably why few if any early homebrew micros used DRAM. Yup, recently built a Mark-8 replica. Currently has 512 bytes of 1101 RAM :) Ahh, ok. I'd known about 1103 RAMs but have never come across anything that used it. Most 8008 microcomputers used 1101 RAM (256-bit static), or later, 2102 RAM (1K static). Oh my gosh, he is such a noodle I might build an 8008 system and use 1103A DRAM to be period-correct.
